## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population size P and time t, which is the fundamental problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from exponential to logistic growth with various extensions including Allee effects, density-dependent mortality, and time-varying parameters.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Malthusian growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (exponential growth, density-independent)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (log-dependent density regulation)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (generalized density dependence)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 + c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Beverton-Holt type: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (rational density dependence)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (flexible sigmoid growth)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * t) (time-varying carrying capacity)
- Exponential decay in rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent intrinsic growth rate)
- Seasonal modulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (periodic environmental forcing)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional-order density dependence)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 + c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Hassell-type: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P)**c2 (generalized contest/scramble competition)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial Allee and saturation effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P â†’ density-independent (Malthusian) growth component; dP/dt ~ c*P
- Quadratic term in P (Pآ²) â†’ pairwise interactions such as intraspecific competition or cooperation (logistic-type density dependence)
- Cubic term in P (Pآ³) â†’ Allee effect combined with carrying capacity, producing bistability in population dynamics
- Logarithmic dependence on P â†’ Gompertz-type regulation where per-capita growth rate declines logarithmically with density
- Rational form P/(1+cP) â†’ contest competition where resources are divided among individuals with diminishing returns
- Multiplicative time-dependent factor â†’ non-autonomous dynamics from environmental change, seasonality, or resource depletion
- Product of two linear factors in P â†’ two critical population thresholds (extinction threshold and carrying capacity)
- Fractional power of P (P^c where 0<c<1) â†’ sub-linear scaling typical of metabolic/allometric constraints on population growth
- Exponential function of time multiplying P-dependent terms â†’ exponentially shifting environmental conditions or resource availability
- Negative quadratic with positive linear term in P â†’ classic hump-shaped growth curve peaking at intermediate population density

## Analysis

Let me first expand the GT numerical expression:

$$0.8678 \cdot P^{1/3} + 0.8678 \cdot P + 0.8678 \cdot (-1 + P/6.058)(1 - P/14.185) \cdot P$$

Let me expand the cubic part:
$$(-1 + P/6.058)(1 - P/14.185) = -1 + P/14.185 + P/6.058 - P^2/(6.058 \times 14.185)$$

Multiplying by $0.8678 \cdot P$:
$$0.8678P \cdot (-1 + P/14.185 + P/6.058 - P^2/85.90)$$

$$= -0.8678P + 0.8678P^2/14.185 + 0.8678P^2/6.058 - 0.8678P^3/85.90$$

Adding the remaining terms $0.8678P^{1/3} + 0.8678P$:

- $P^{1/3}$ term: $0.8678$
- $P$ terms: $0.8678 - 0.8678 = 0$ (they cancel!)
- $P^2$ terms: $0.8678/14.185 + 0.8678/6.058 = 0.06118 + 0.14324 = 0.20442$
- $P^3$ term: $-0.8678/85.90 = -0.01010$

So the GT simplifies to:
$$0.8678 \cdot P^{1/3} + 0.20442 \cdot P^2 - 0.01010 \cdot P^3$$

This is of the form: $a \cdot P^{1/3} + b \cdot P^2 + c \cdot P^3$

Now looking at the candidates:

**Candidate 10**: $P^{1/3} \cdot c_0 + P^3 \cdot c_1 + P^2 \cdot c_2$

This is exactly $c_0 \cdot P^{1/3} + c_1 \cdot P^3 + c_2 \cdot P^2$

Setting:
- $c_0 = 0.8678$
- $c_1 = -0.01010$
- $c_2 = 0.20442$

This matches the GT perfectly!

Let me verify the P term cancellation more carefully:
- From the product: coefficient of P is $0.8678 \times (-1) = -0.8678$
- From $c_7 \cdot P$: $+0.8678$
- Total: $0$

Yes, the linear term in P vanishes exactly, confirming that the GT reduces to $P^{1/3} + P^2 + P^3$ terms only.

**Candidate 10** matches the Ground Truth.

`0.8677806610632854*(-1 + P/6.057935627201261)*(1 - P/14.185052779605893)*P + 0.8677806610632854*P**0.333333333333333 + 0.8677806610632854*P`

Let me expand the first term:
`(-1 + P/6.058)*(1 - P/14.185)*P`

Let me denote a = 6.058, b = 14.185 for brevity.

`(-1 + P/a)*(1 - P/b)*P = (P/a - 1)*(1 - P/b)*P`

Expanding `(P/a - 1)*(1 - P/b)`:
= `P/a - Pآ²/(ab) - 1 + P/b`
= `-1 + P(1/a + 1/b) - Pآ²/(ab)`

Multiplying by P:
= `-P + Pآ²(1/a + 1/b) - Pآ³/(ab)`

So the GT becomes:
`c * [-P + Pآ²(1/a + 1/b) - Pآ³/(ab)] + c*P^(1/3) + c*P`

where c = 0.8678.

= `c*P^(1/3) + c*P - c*P + c*Pآ²(1/a + 1/b) - c*Pآ³/(ab)`

The `-c*P` and `+c*P` cancel!

**GT = c*P^(1/3) + c*(1/a + 1/b)*Pآ² - c/(ab)*Pآ³**

So GT has the form:
**GT = A*P^(1/3) + B*Pآ² + C*Pآ³**

where:
- A = c â‰ˆ 0.8678
- B = c*(1/a + 1/b) â‰ˆ 0.8678*(0.16507 + 0.07050) â‰ˆ 0.8678*0.23557 â‰ˆ 0.2044
- C = -c/(ab) â‰ˆ -0.8678/(85.91) â‰ˆ -0.01010
